## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and possibly time t, which is the standard second-order ODE form for (non)linear oscillators. Typical physics relationships combine a restoring force in x, damping in v, and optional time-dependent forcing/parametric modulation in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = -(c0 * x) (Hooke-law restoring acceleration, no damping/forcing)
- Constant-acceleration bias: dv_dt = c0 - (c1 * x) (equilibrium shift or gravity-like bias plus linear stiffness)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = -(c0 * x) - (c1 * v) (damped SHO)
- Linear stiffness with quadratic drag: dv_dt = -(c0 * x) - (c1 * v * Abs(v)) (aerodynamic drag-like damping)
- Coulomb (dry) friction: dv_dt = -(c0 * x) - (c1 * sign(v)) (sliding friction approximation; often smoothed with tanh(c*v))
- Duffing (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -(c0 * x) - (c1 * x**3) (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Damped Duffing: dv_dt = -(c0 * x) - (c1 * x**3) - (c2 * v) (nonlinear stiffness + viscous damping)
- Quintic stiffness (higher-order): dv_dt = -(c0 * x) - (c1 * x**3) - (c2 * x**5) (strongly nonlinear restoring force)
- Simple pendulum (geometric nonlinearity): dv_dt = -(c0 * sin(c1 * x)) - (c2 * v) (bounded restoring term vs x)
- Driven oscillator: dv_dt = -(c0 * x) - (c1 * v) + (c2 * cos(c3 * t)) (external periodic forcing)
- Mathieu / parametric excitation: dv_dt = -((c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x) - (c3 * v) (time-modulated stiffness; parametric resonance)
- Van der Pol oscillator (nonlinear damping / limit cycle): dv_dt = -(c0 * x) + (c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v) (negative damping at small |x|, positive at large |x|)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-nonlinear damping): dv_dt = -(c0 * x) + (c1 * (c2 - v**2) * v) (self-excited oscillations via v-dependent damping)
- Potential-gradient form (conservative): dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) (interpretable as dv_dt = -dU/dx with polynomial U(x))

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative oscillator signature: dv_dt depends on x only (no v, no explicit t), often an odd function of x for symmetric potentials (e.g., x, x**3, sin(c*x)).
- Linear viscous damping signature: additive term proportional to v; causes exponential decay of oscillation amplitude in time-domain solutions.
- Drag/friction regimes: v*Abs(v) indicates quadratic drag; sign(v) (or tanh(c*v) as a smooth proxy) indicates dry friction with nearly constant-magnitude deceleration.
- Hardening vs softening stiffness: positive cubic stiffness term (-(c*x**3) with c>0) typically hardens (frequency increases with amplitude); negative cubic stiffness softens.
- Bounded restoring force: sin(c*x) implies a restoring acceleration that saturates for large |x|, typical of pendulum-like geometry.
- External forcing indicator: explicit periodic functions of t (cos(c*t), sin(c*t)) added to dv_dt produce entrainment and resonance near the natural frequency.
- Parametric excitation indicator: time-periodic coefficient multiplying x (e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x) produces instability tongues and parametric resonance.
- Self-excited limit-cycle indicator: damping coefficient changes sign with state magnitude, e.g., (c0 - x**2)*v or (c0 - v**2)*v, yielding growth at small amplitude and saturation at large amplitude.
- Symmetry check: if the physics is symmetric under x -> -x, then dv_dt should be odd in x and even in v for conservative parts; asymmetries suggest bias terms (constants) or asymmetric friction.

A candidate can match iff we can set its free constants so that it reduces **exactly** to
\[

with \(A=-1.16984597672115\), \(B=-0.661172493025524\), \(C=-0.330586246512762\), and all extra terms vanish identically (not just approximately). Also, \(\log(c\,|v|+1)\) can only equal \(\log(|v|+1)\) for all \(v\) if \(c=1\).

### 2. `... + c2*sin(...) + c5*log(...)`
Set sine amplitude \(c2=0\). Then same as (1): set \(c6=1\), \(c0,c1,c5\) to GT coefficients. Ō£ģ Matches.

### 3. `... + c4*log(c5*exp(c6*x) + 1)`

### 4. `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*v + c3*x**c4*cos(c5*t) + c6*sin(c7*log(...)+c9)`
Need no \(t\)-dependence and no extra trig: set \(c3=0\) and \(c6=0\). Also remove linear \(x\): set \(c0=0\). Then set \(c1,c2\) to GT \(x^3\) and \(v\) coefficients, and add missing log term? There is **no plain log term**, only inside the killed sine. With \(c6=0\), log disappears entirely, so cannot match GTŌĆÖs \(\log(|v|+1)\) term. ŌØī No match.

### 5. `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*v*sin(...) + c6*log(...)`
To get linear \(v\) term, the `v*sin(...)` is problematic unless it becomes exactly \(v\) for all \(x,t\), which is impossible (a sine cannot be identically 1 for all \(x,t\)). Only option is \(c2=0\), but then no \(v\) term except none. So cannot match. ŌØī

### 6. `... + c2*x + c3*x*sin(...) + ...`
Kill extra \(x\) terms: set \(c2=0,c3=0\). Then it becomes (1)-type; set \(c7=1\) and coefficients to GT. Ō£ģ Matches.

### 7. `... + c2*v + c3*v*x**2 + ...`

### 10. `... + c3*exp(c4*Abs(x))*log(c5*Abs(v) + 1)`

Let me analyze each candidate systematically. The key question for each is whether the extra terms beyond `x┬│`, `v`, and `log(Abs(v)+1)` can be zeroed out or absorbed.

Set c4=0, c5=0. Then it becomes `c0*x┬│ + c1*v + c2*log(c3*|v|+1)`. With c3=1, this matches GT.
**Candidate 1 verdict: [MATCH]**
